All slow moving pistol rounds and even slower arrow that did have a heavy projectile. Projectiles work two ways, oneâ€¦ big heavy projectile acts like a hammer and breaks through. Twoâ€¦ a very fast moving smaller projectile penetrates due to really the speeds and not so much the mass of the projectile. So most pistol rounds which is all he listed off as even the old school Thompson Submachine gun(Tommy gun)shoots a standard .45 ACP pistol round. A slow moving heavier projectile at usually always subsonic speeds. Most all pistol rounds will be at or below 1,300 FPS(feet per second)which is relatively slow compared to even the slower rifle rounds that will start off at double the speeds of a pistol round(except of course for a few select self defense rounds made or hand loads). Hilarious loved it. But I am not surprised with the result b/c that is the wrong arrowhead for metal. You need to use a medieval-style warbodkin. Arrows like the "Crecy" or Type 9 war bodkin (Lond museum designation)  They would have a better chance of penetrating b/c they don't curl on impact like your broadhead. They were designed for precisely this task (armour penetration).  Not saying they will go through 100%,  but they are the arrowheads you need to use for hitting that type of material.   A 150lb English Warbow or a 110-130 Macnhu style Warbow will produce the same energy as your 90lb 520/grain @300fps arrow (140j ke).  However, they will do it with a heavier arrow (moving slower of course) but b/c the arrow is so heavy it will have more momentum which is great for penetrating armor.  A 110lb @34" Tiron bow my Misko Rovcanin Bows will shoot a 1530 grain arrow at 175 fps for 141 j(ke) and 5.29k m/s of momentum.  Your 90lb compound will also generate 140j but only 3.081 kg m/s of momentum. I would love to see someone try that.  .

Elon claims a .45 has more penetration than a 9mm round and I would love to bet him($1 or more if he accepts) that he is wrong. I personally tested a bullet proof vest sample with a number of rounds. The 9mm hollow point penetrated 2 layers of material(kevlar) more than the .45 and 2 or 3 layers less than a 9mm ball round. A .223 went right through like butter, through 2 telephone books and then about 14" into hard desert ground.12 gauge birdshot was stopped on the first layer but made the vest sample disappear into the phone book(at point blank). I also tested a .45(ball) in my buddy's 12' pool. Mythbuster's erroneously said that you are safe under water if someone is shooting at you. Wrong! .223/5.56 disintegrates and turns into small shrapnel almost at the surface(but I think they should've tested different angles. In my test we shot a .45 at a 45 degree angle and it hit the 12' bottom hard enough to dent the bullet and the bottom of the pool, bounced up a couple feet and slowly fell back down. We were pretty sure it would penetrate a body. But I wanna give Elon the benefit of the doubt that he is partially correct. He mentioned his .45 tests were done with a Tommy gun. So with a longer barrel than a 9mm pistol I'm assuming the .45 had more velocity and more penetration.

the size and weight of the bolt vs the arrow is not relevant unless they are both going the same velocity. A Crossbow can hit 450FPS. The Momentum (not force) is Mass times Velocity. (Force would be Mass times acceleration and that would measure how much force was applied to the projectile, but I am more interested in the moment each has After it reaches it's peak velocity and then hits the cybertruck)   Joe says his Arrow is  520 grains @ 300FPS. A Crossbow bolt is anywhere from 400 to 450, and will do up to 450 FPS.  So without bothering to convert anything... Joes arrow will have momentum of 300 * 520 which is 156,000 of...some unit.  Elons Crossbow would have momentum of 450 * 450 which is 202,500  or like 23% more of whatever the heck this unit of measure is.  Thus the bolt will impart a greater impact to the cybertruck. Classy.

Side impacts, also known as T-bone or broadside collisions, occur when a vehicle is struck on its side. These types of accidents can be very serious.   Side impacts can be dangerous because the side of a vehicle offers less protection compared to the front or rear. The force of the impact can directly affect the passenger compartment, potentially causing severe injuries to the occupants. Here are some key points to consider:  1. Occupant Protection: In side impacts, the head, chest, and abdomen are particularly vulnerable to injury. This is because there is less space and structural reinforcement on the sides of vehicles compared to the front and rear. Injuries can include head trauma, rib fractures, internal organ damage, spinal injuries, and pelvic fractures.  2. Safety Features: To help mitigate the effects of side impacts, Elons car is bulletproof.  3. Structural Reinforcement: Tesla trucks have implemented reinforced side structures to enhance the vehicle's ability to absorb and distribute the impact forces. These reinforcements are usually placed in the doors, pillars, and roof to provide additional protection and maintain the integrity of the passenger compartment.

It is likely a 125 -140 grain broadhead with thin blades, openings, and a thin long center point.  NOW if Joe had used a field tip.  That 125 - 140 grain would be condensed into one solid point with NO place to crumple. A crossbow BOLT is radically different from a crossbow QUARREL. A quarrel is like a mini arrow, made of the same stuff as an arrow, only shorter. A BOLT is a heavy projectile, usually cast in one piece, out of steel or iron, fired from a heavy crossbow, the kind you have to crank a wheel for a minute and a half to charge. A three-pound bolt fired from a heavy crossbow like the kind I just described, will go in one side and out the other of the cybertruck like it wasn't even there. They were designed to break through stone and they work very well.
